## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (continuous-time population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by the current population P and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics models (per-capita growth, density dependence, seasonality, harvesting/immigration).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Time-varying intrinsic growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (secular trend in environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Periodic/seasonal forcing: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (seasonal variation in per-capita growth)
- Power-law per-capita growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric or phenomenological scaling; c1>1 can yield accelerating growth)
- Finite-time blow-up (hyperbolic) form: dP_dt = c0 * P**2 (simple positive feedback; can approximate autocatalytic-like population increase)
- Crowding via quadratic self-limitation: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (c1 < 0 produces density-dependent suppression)
- Generalized self-limitation (theta-logistic / Richards-type ODE): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density dependence; includes logistic-like behavior as a special case)
- Gompertz-type growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines ~ log(P); common for microbial/tumor growth)
- Von Bertalanffy / surface-limited form: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (net growth from anabolic term minus catabolic loss; often c1 < 1)
- Saturating per-capita growth (crowding with asymptotic cap on dP_dt/P): dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (resource limitation modeled as a rational saturation)
- Strong overcompensation (Ricker-like continuous analogue): dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (fast decline of per-capita growth at high density)
- Allee effect (depensation) with crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - (c2 * P)**c3) (negative growth at low P plus high-density limitation)
- Harvesting/constant removal with growth: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 (constant yield harvesting/stocking offset)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P (net intrinsic growth minus linear loss)
- Time-dependent carrying pressure: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * P) (seasonal changes in effective crowding term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is proportional to P (dP_dt ≈ c * P), then per-capita growth (dP_dt/P) is constant → density-independent exponential regime.
- If dP_dt/P decreases approximately linearly with P, expect a self-limiting structure like c0*P + c1*P**2 (crowding via quadratic term).
- If per-capita growth declines with log(P), a log(c/P) factor is typical → Gompertz-like dynamics and asymmetric approach to an upper size.
- If growth accelerates superlinearly with P (power > 1), positive feedback is indicated → terms like c0*P**c1 with c1>1.
- If dP_dt/P saturates to a maximum at low P but is suppressed at high P, rational forms c0*P/(1+c1*P) capture diminishing marginal gains.
- If low-density populations decline (dP_dt < 0 for small P) but recover above a threshold, include an Allee factor (c1*P - 1) multiplying P.
- If growth shows periodic waxing/waning in time at fixed P, include sinusoidal modulation in t inside the per-capita rate (c0 + c1*sin(c2*t + c3)).
- If external inputs/removals exist independent of P (stocking/constant harvest), include additive constants (±c0) in dP_dt rather than only multiplicative P terms.
- If suppression at high density is sharper than polynomial (rapid crash), exponential-in-P damping exp(-c*P) is a common phenomenological signature.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(t, P) = 0.1404 \cdot (-1 + P/4.532) \cdot (1 - P/78.49) \cdot P + 0.1404 \cdot P / t^{4.532}$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) = -1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)$$

So the GT becomes:
$$0.1404 \cdot P \cdot \left(-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)\right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

$$= 0.1404 \cdot \left(-P + P^2/78.49 + P^2/4.532 - P^3/(355.7) \right) + 0.1404 \cdot P \cdot t^{-4.532}$$

The GT has the form:
$$\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P + \delta P \cdot t^{-\epsilon}$$

where $\alpha, \beta, \gamma, \delta, \epsilon$ are specific constants. This is a **cubic polynomial in P** plus a **$P \cdot t^{-c}$ term**.

The basis functions in GT are: $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$, and $P \cdot t^{-c}$ (where $c \approx 4.532$).

Now let me check each candidate:

### Candidate 1: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 (c_3 + t)^{c_4} + P^{c_5} c_6$

This has $P^2$, $P$, $P(c_3+t)^{c_4}$, and $P^{c_5}$. The term $P(c_3+t)^{c_4}$ with $c_3=0, c_4=-4.532$ gives $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$. The term $P^{c_5}$ with $c_5=3$ gives $P^3$. So we get $P^3, P^2, P, P \cdot t^{-4.532}$ — this matches the GT basis functions!

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

Has exponentials in P — can't match cubic polynomial. Even setting exp coefficients to 0, we'd have $P \cdot t^{c_1} + P + P^{c_2}c_3 + c_8$. With $c_2=3$, this gives $P^3 + P + P t^{c_1} + c_8$, missing $P^2$ and has unwanted constant $c_8$. Setting $c_8=0$, still missing $P^2$.
